# Putting ITIL® into Practice: Problem Management Techniques

> Problem management is about preventing and resolving the problems underlying interruptions of IT services. A set of shared techniques can make the difference between success and failure. ITIL® mentions a set of techniques as a best practice, but does not cover how to apply them. This course bridges the gap for IT pros, giving them a concise introduction to the seven problem management techniques e

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448) | 2h 38m | Intermediate | 103K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

#### Stand apart as a problem practitioner
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/stand-apart-as-a-problem-practitioner?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/stand-apart-as-a-problem-practitioner?u=76281980&t=0)** - Isn't it strange?
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/stand-apart-as-a-problem-practitioner?u=76281980&t=1)** People in organizations expect you to have problem management skills, yet most people never get formal training in them.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/stand-apart-as-a-problem-practitioner?u=76281980&t=7)** And teams of top troubleshooters can struggle without a shared approach, leading to chaos, miscommunication, and half-baked solutions.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/stand-apart-as-a-problem-practitioner?u=76281980&t=15)** So don't be that person, lead real solutions.

> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/stand-apart-as-a-problem-practitioner?u=76281980&t=31)** Join me, elevate your career, become the go-to problem solver your team needs.

#### What is problem management?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's start with what we mean by a problem.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=3)** You should see from this definition that it's not the same as an incident.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=8)** In fact, you can think of an incident as the symptom of a problem.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=11)** For example, if 800 people contact the service desk today because their shared folders and drives have disappeared, each contact represents an incident.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=20)** The unknown underlying cause of these incidents is a problem.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=25)** ITIL defines four dimensions that make up services and where you can look for causes and solutions for problems.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=31)** Organizations and people, information and technology, partners and suppliers, and value streams and processes.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=38)** Use these dimensions as you see causes of and solutions for problems.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=43)** Doing so will make your approach more ITIL aligned and your analyses more complete.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=48)** As you can see here, services are made up by the four dimensions.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=52)** Services experience problems like outages or poor response time due to issues in or among components in each dimension.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=60)** To minimize the occurrence and impact of problems and solve them, you must consider each dimension as you seek possible causes and solutions.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=69)** You should see from this definition that the proper scope of your practice must be problem management, not just problem solving.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=77)** Problem management has a larger scope that includes proactively minimizing the occurrence and impact of problems, improving how you react to problems, and getting to the root cause and resolution quicker.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=89)** You achieve this by continually improving your practice by applying lessons learned.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=95)** One word of caution.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=97)** You must never jump to solutions without sufficient facts and always be thorough enough and look for causes and solutions in the four dimensions.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=105)** But you must also not fall into the analysis paralysis trap where you take so much time researching problems and seeking optimal perfect data and decisions that you either take no action or take it too late, increasing the negative impact of problems on your stakeholders.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=122)** When seeking the causes of and solutions for problems, aim for just enough analysis to gain sufficient insight and spur timely action rather than for perfect insight.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=133)** Do this because the effectiveness of your decisions and actions is time bound, like a mariner's decision to change course.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=139)** The sooner you resolve, the sooner your stakeholders will see the benefits.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=144)** Part of managing problems is driving towards a better reality by isolating and eliminating the causes of problems, but getting better reality isn't enough.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=153)** You must also seek better perception by showing stakeholders that you have a firm grasp on what the problem is or was, what you've done, are doing, and will do about it.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=163)** Who's doing what by when, and why.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-problem-management?u=76281980&t=166)** And that you are taking steps to prevent and better handle future problems.

#### A consistent set of techniques
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Idle mentions and is not the author of the problem techniques covered here.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=4)** Techniques were created by different people at different times for different purposes.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=8)** So naturally, some inconsistencies exist among them, such as in their categorization and prioritization schemes, and steps for action and communication.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=17)** These variations unnecessarily will hinder you and your team from adopting and using them as a set.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=23)** To address this, I've rationalized these differences across the seven techniques to make them easier for you and your team to adopt and apply.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=30)** I've aligned them to use idles four dimensions in their categorization schemes, to use a single shared prioritization scheme, and to include mitigations and contingencies when seeking countermeasures, and include a consistent set of preparation, communication, action, and review steps.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=47)** The common prioritization framework is to rank based on three key dimensions.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=51)** Impact, how significantly does the issue affect business safety, system performance, or user experiences?
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=59)** Probability, what's the likelihood associated with it?
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=62)** And effort, how much time, cost, and resources will it require?
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=68)** Here is the prioritization scheme shared across the techniques.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=72)** Assign a weight to impact probability and effort.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=75)** Rate each item on a scale of one to five for each of the three factors.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=78)** I've included a suggested starting weight for each.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=81)** Adjust each factor's weight based on your context.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=84)** Use the scores for each weighted factor to calculate a weighted priority for each item, then sort items with higher scores as higher priority.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=93)** I've rationalized the techniques to consider mitigations and contingencies when seeking risk countermeasures.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=99)** Mitigations are things you put in place to prevent situations from occurring in the first place, like, using fireproof materials to reduce the risk of fire.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=108)** Contingencies are things you put in place to respond effectively and minimize the impact of a situation when the risk does occur, like installing fire extinguishers to put out fires.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=119)** Throughout this course, you'll see the same example of a collaboration service used as the basis for exercising each technique.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/a-consisistent-set-of-techniques?u=76281980&t=126)** Using a single example with a detailed reference should help you better know the scope and applicability of each technique, how they fit together, and how you can use them as a set in your problem management practice.

#### What you'll learn
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Idle's coverage of the seven techniques you'll learn here isn't very deep.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=4)** It simply mentions them but doesn't tell you how to do them.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=7)** In this course, you'll learn the what, why, and how of each technique, improving your ability to prevent problems in the first place, and to respond more effectively when they do occur, and influence others to adopt them, and show them how.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=22)** In this course, you'll learn the what, why, and how of seven problem management techniques so you can begin to apply them.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=27)** There are more variations and details for these techniques than it makes sense to cover in this course.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=32)** So at the end of the course, I'll cover where to go and what to do to continue your problem management journey.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=38)** The first technique we'll cover is brainstorming.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=40)** It's a collaborative idea-generating method where people contribute ideas in a round robin fashion until people or ideas are exhausted.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=48)** The goal, keep the ideas flowing until the team loses momentum or hits a breakthrough.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=54)** It's not about filtering or critiquing, it's about generating as many good ideas as possible.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=59)** Use it to quickly generate ideas for problem causes and solutions under time pressure.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=65)** The next technique you'll learn is cause-effect analysis, which produces a visual of cause and effect relationships.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=71)** These diagrams are also known as Ishikawa diagrams after their creator, Kaoru Ishikawa, or tree or fishbone diagrams, you map causes and effects, the resulting chart looks like a tree's branches, and spurs, or a fish's bones.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=86)** Kepner-Tregoe analysis is a structured approach to finding a problem's root cause in four phases, describing the problem, identifying possible causes, evaluating possible causes, and confirming the actual cause.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=99)** The power of the Kepner-Tregoe method is its simplicity and rigor.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=103)** It helps ensure that you as a team nail down causes before jumping to solutions.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=109)** Fault tree analysis is a technique to identify that chain of events that has caused or may cause a problem, such as a service outage or performance degradation.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=118)** It links essential, resultant, conditional, and trigger events using boolean logic operators and, or, xor, and the like to illustrate event change and the logic behind them graphically.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=131)** The best way to prevent problems is to understand what could fail or go wrong, and then work to minimize or eliminate those possibilities.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=138)** Component failure impact analysis is a technique where you map service components to identify single points of failure so that you can establish the right degree of failover capabilities.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=148)** Use it as the basis for increasing the resilience of your services and infrastructure.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=153)** Service outage analysis is where you review why one or more services failed, identify root causes, analyze trends, and find ways to prevent future outages.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=164)** Instead of just fixing what's broke, you ask how you can stop the outage from happening again.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=170)** You study past outages to improve service stability, resilience, and quality, and turn failures into lessons that drive continuous improvement.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=179)** In a problem review, you analyze a problem in its aftermath, breaking down what happened, and why.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=186)** You aim to identify actions, prevent a similar situation from occurring, and to handle it better if it does.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-you-ll-learn?u=76281980&t=192)** Use it to identify root causes, what you did in your response that worked well and didn't, lessons learned, action items for improvement, and stakeholder communication plans.

>

>

>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=44)** Under why do it, you'll learn the technique's purpose, what it is intended to produce or achieve.
>

>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=54)** Others must understand what's in it for them to be passionate enough to begin applying the technique.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=60)** You will only be able to achieve breakthroughs and capability when your team adopts them as a shared technique with each person having a baseline understanding and facility with them.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=71)** You'll also learn the technique scope, its applicability boundaries or limits, and the situations in which it is and is not applicable.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=79)** Knowing this will help you choose which technique to apply to a particular situation and avoid applying a technique that doesn't fit the situation and the outcomes you seek.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=89)** In the end, you must understand the steps you must take to apply the technique and how to execute them.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=94)** You must know what the artifacts associated with the method are and how to use them to produce the outputs and outcomes you seek.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=101)** That is what you'll learn under how to do it.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=105)** Each how to do it segment will also include a worked example to help you see the method applied step by step to help you bridge the gap between theory and practice.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=114)** The examples are designed to make it easier for you to use the technique in similar situations and to explain the technique to others.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=122)** In the do it phase, you'll try each technique to get them into muscle memory before using them in real world situations where it counts.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/how-you-ll-learn-it?u=76281980&t=130)** Ideally, you'll do this in a team setting because the real power of these techniques comes when they're used and shared together.

#### Building capacity
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Think of how firefighters drill to prepare for fires, where decisive actions, quick responses, calm, temperament, and seamless collaboration become second nature.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=10)** Getting things into muscle memory where actions and reactions are second nature and come about naturally is what that's all about.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=18)** You want to avoid common pitfalls when you and your team work to build your problem management capability.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=24)** The first is simply to intellectually accept the need for building capability, but not doing the practice and drills required to achieve and sustain it.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=33)** The other is where the collective organization lacks capability, even when made up of competent individuals and teams.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=40)** This happens when the team lacks shared practices.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=43)** True capability is like a fire brigade's ability to respond to a fire.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=47)** The time to settle on shared practices and get them into muscle memory is well before the fire is burning.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=54)** Firefighters do not wait to figure out whether they should be putting on their boots before or after their pants when the alarm bell rings.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=61)** Similarly, you cannot afford to wait until a crisis to determine and build the capabilities you need.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=67)** Instead, you must build capability into muscle memory through drills, exercise, and practice.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=74)** In the Do It phase, you try these techniques for yourself, with your team if possible, because the real power in these techniques comes when they're shared and the collective has them in muscle memory.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=85)** Aim to be fluent with the techniques as a group before you need them, so you hit the ground running when you do.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=92)** After you do it, review it.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=95)** You'll ask yourself and your team these questions.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=98)** What happened?
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=99)** What does it mean?
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=100)** What actions will we take on what we've experienced and learned?
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=104)** Will we adopt this technique?
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=106)** Do we have the passion to practice it and get it into muscle memory as a team?
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=112)** So now you know what a problem and problem management are and that you'll learn seven problem management techniques in this course: brainstorming, cause-effect analysis, Kepner-Tregoe analysis, fault tree analysis, component failure impact analysis, service outage analysis, and problem review.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/building-capacity?u=76281980&t=130)** In the next video, you'll learn the first technique: brainstorming.

### 1. Brainstorming

#### What is brainstorming, and why use it?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=0)** - Brainstorming is a collaborative idea generating method of shared problem solving in which all team members contribute ideas.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=6)** In a round robin fashion, each person contributes ideas in turn until the team runs out of ideas or energy to continue.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=14)** The goal, keep the ideas flowing until the team loses momentum or hits a breakthrough.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=20)** It's not about filtering or critiquing, it's about quickly generating many good ideas.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=25)** Why use brainstorming and problem management?
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=27)** Because speed and collaboration matter and problem management time is tight.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=32)** You need a flood of diverse, high quality ideas.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=34)** Fast brainstorming gets everyone involved, unlocking creativity and surfacing high quality solutions.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=41)** And it's not just about ideas, it's about buy-in.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=44)** When people contribute, they're invested.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=47)** That drives alignment, better decisions, and real action.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=51)** Brainstorming isn't just about throwing ideas on a board.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=54)** It's a structured approach to smarter problem solving, stronger communication, and continuous improvement.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-brainstorming-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=60)** Use it, master it, solve problems better together.

>
> **Frameworks & Libraries:** [[Problem Management]] (2)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)

#### Where and when to use brainstorming
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Use brainstorming when you are in a thinking rut to boost the quality and diversity of ideas.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=5)** Use it to include different perspectives, creativity, and uncover solutions that a single viewpoint might miss.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=12)** The one significant rule of brainstorming is, no idea is criticized ever.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=18)** This rule helps create an atmosphere free from judgment, allowing people to be creative and develop ideas they wouldn't have otherwise.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=25)** Brainstorming isn't just about ideas.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=27)** It's about being heard.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=29)** The loudest and most forceful voices shouldn't lead, and the quietest shouldn't fade.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=34)** It would be a shame if someone couldn't get airtime to voice good ideas.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=38)** Brainstorming structure allows all to participate and prevents any one viewpoint from drowning out others, because the best ideas can come from anyone if they get the chance to speak.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=49)** Use brainstorming to prevent people from hatching ideas in isolation.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=53)** This can result in a team spending time and energy advocating for competing ideas rather than co-creating them.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=60)** A core benefit of brainstorming is that everyone can contribute ideas and build on others.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=65)** This helps you choose the best ideas to move forward with and creates buy-in as a natural byproduct, because when you contribute to ideas, you see them as your baby.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=76)** When time is tight, brainstorming delivers, rapid fire ideas, no overthinking, just solutions fast, diverse minds, quick insights, unexpected breakthroughs.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=87)** It cuts through delays, sparks innovation and gets you to action, because in problem management, speed matters, but so does getting it right.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=98)** When problems strike, use brainstorming to find causes, workarounds, and solutions.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=103)** In fast-paced environments where problems must be resolved quickly, brainstorming provides an efficient, structured way to gather facts and identify possible causes and solutions.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=112)** It is especially useful when the issue is ongoing and requires immediate action.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=119)** Before problems strike, proactively brainstorm mitigations and contingencies for likely problems.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=124)** Then, take steps to minimize or eliminate their occurrence and their impacts should they occur.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=131)** Mitigations are things you put in place to prevent situations from occurring in the first place, like using fireproof materials to reduce the chance of fire starting.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=142)** Contingencies are things you put in place to respond effectively and minimize the impact of a situation when it does occur.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=148)** Like installing fire extinguishers to put out fires should they occur.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=154)** In the aftermath of problems, use it to agree and communicate what went wrong and what you've done and will do to minimize the likelihood and impact of a similar problem occurring, and how you'll do better next time if it does occur.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=167)** In a problem review, after a problem has been resolved, it's important to quickly understand and come to a consensus on what went wrong and how can we do better next time.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=176)** Brainstorming is great for that.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=178)** Ask brainstorming questions in the four dimensions to help ensure you've covered all the bases.

#### Brainstorming steps
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The steps in brainstorming are: pick a facilitator, team, and tools; agree on the brainstorming question; go around, share ideas, and write them down; review, clarify, and remove duplicates; choose actions and set a review date; plan stakeholder communications; communicate findings to stakeholders; take action and track progress; review progress and adjust as needed; and share updates and lessons learned.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=26)** Select a facilitator to record ideas, uphold rules, and maintain focus on generating not judging ideas and ensuring all voices are heard.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=36)** Assemble a team with the right combination of expertise to contribute, challenge, expand on, and refine ideas.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=43)** Then select and set up the necessary tools like whiteboards, markers, and sticky notes for the in-person sessions or digital collaboration tools for remote discussions.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=53)** Good brainstorming starts with getting the question right.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=56)** A well-formed question is clear, focused, and open-ended, broad enough to encourage creative ideas but specific enough to keep the discussion on track.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=64)** Write it down to align the team and so that you can adjust it explicitly if needed.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=69)** Gain agreement that it's the right question to pursue.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=72)** Does it target the right challenge?
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=74)** Will it lead to actionable solutions?
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=76)** If not, refine it.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=78)** A great question sets the stage for great ideas.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=83)** Start by writing down the first big rule of brainstorming: No idea is criticized, ever.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=89)** This rule is meant to create an atmosphere free from criticism and judgment to free people up to be creative and to bring ideas that they otherwise wouldn't have surfaced.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=99)** Next, write down the second big rule: Everyone contributes in turn.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=103)** This rule ensures that all voices are heard, preventing dominant voices from taking over.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=108)** It encourages tabling divergent ideas and giving quieter participants a chance to share.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=114)** The facilitator plays a key role by keeping the discussion moving and ensuring no one gets overlooked.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=120)** The goal is to keep the flow of ideas balanced and inclusive, leading to more creative solutions.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=127)** With the questions locked in, it's time to generate ideas round-robin style.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=132)** Each person shares one idea per turn, no interruptions, no debates.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=136)** The facilitator writes each idea down, big, clear, and visible so nothing gets lost.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=141)** The golden rule, no criticism ever.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=144)** Every idea gets spaced to breathe.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=147)** The process continues, cycling through the team until everyone passes or the energy runs out.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=151)** The goal isn't to judge, it's to get everything out there.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=155)** And here's the key, no editing in real time.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=158)** Even if ideas are fuzzy or repeated, flow first and filter later.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=163)** During idea generation, resist the urge to edit.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=166)** Some ideas will be unclear or repeated, and that's okay.

> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=169)** Stopping to refine or combine ideas too soon breaks the flow and shuts down creativity.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=175)** The goal right now is quantity not perfection.

>

>

>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=260)** Ensure the right people know what happened, what's next, and why it matters.

>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=270)** Choose the messengers and the channels they trust, like email, meetings, and dashboards.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=276)** Keep communication clear, concise, and two-way.
>

>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=294)** Tell stakeholders what's happening, why, and who's responsible.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=298)** Summarize the actions.

>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=302)** Because reality improves with action and perception improves with good communication.
>

>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=319)** Build and sustained momentum.
>

>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=322)** Turn your plans into results.
>

>

> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=327)** Meeting deadlines?
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=329)** Gather feedback.
>
> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=330)** What's working and what's not?
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=332)** Look at the data.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=333)** Spot gaps.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=335)** If needed, refine actions, shift priorities, or reassign tasks.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=339)** Progress isn't about motion, it's about direction.
>

>

>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=348)** Share it.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=349)** Keep stakeholders informed with meetings, reports, or collaboration tools.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=354)** Transparency builds trust.
>
> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=356)** Show them what's working, what's changed, and what's next?
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=359)** Lessons learned, capture them.
>
> **[6:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=361)** Avoid repeating mistakes.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-steps?u=76281980&t=363)** Keep improving.

> **Frameworks & Libraries:** next (5), [[Accountability]] (1), teams (1), [[Dashboards]] (1), [[Trello]] (1)
> **Prerequisites:** set up (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Brainstorming example
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] Now that you've seen the steps to brainstorming, let's examine a real-world example to help reinforce what you've learned.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=7)** Nexiko Lab's IT group wants to brainstorm the components and dependencies of its collaboration service as part of proactive problem management.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=15)** A big part of problem management is to put things in place to prevent problems in the first place or recover faster should a problem occur.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=22)** In this example, the team wants to prevent and recover faster from collaboration services outages.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=28)** The map will help them do that.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=31)** Alex, the PM, picks Jamie, a senior engineer, to facilitate, as he can keep things on track and ensure everyone's voice is heard.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=38)** Alex brings in Priah from the backend, Mark from DevOps, Luis from networking, and Sarah from operations for all necessary perspectives.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=47)** Jamie chooses a whiteboard and digital tools to capture decisions, actions, and communications, making it easy for the team to collaborate and stay on track.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=56)** They start by formulating the brainstorming question.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=58)** Jamie writes it down on the whiteboard: What are the core components of the collaboration service and their dependencies, and how can we reduce downtime and speed up recovery?
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=67)** Priah suggests refining it to include failure points.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=70)** Mark agrees but emphasizes prioritizing fixes.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=74)** After a quick discussion, the team finalizes the question to ensure the scope is clear before proceeding.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=79)** The team begins contributing ideas in turn.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=82)** As ideas are contributed, the facilitator writes each one down.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=85)** Priah starts by listing the backend services, highlighting database interactions, and Luis maps out networking dependencies pointing to the API gateways.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=95)** Mark adds DevOps tools like monitoring and deployment pipelines.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=99)** Sarah shares insights from past outages, emphasizing areas with frequent failures.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=104)** Jamie records everything in Miro to keep ideas visible for everyone.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=109)** People call out components like storage, server roles, servers, and applications in no particular order.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=116)** When the team runs out of ideas or energy, it's time to move on to the editing phase.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=121)** Now the team works to clarify group ideas and eliminate duplicates.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=128)** In this case, the team moves technology services under our new heading, Services, along with the support services which had been under software.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=136)** The people category was replaced with a customer category, and only business units and user classes were kept under these.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=142)** Some in the room needed clarification from others on the nature of some of the components; for example, that server roles are services Service can run, like DNS, AD, DHCP and so on.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=155)** The main objective of all this brainstorming is to produce a list of action items: who will do what and by when.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=162)** In this case, there were several open questions on the standard settings for network routers, the terms of support agreements from suppliers supporting Service, and the particulars around a new storage device class.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=172)** Action items were assigned to get answers.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=176)** The team drafts a summary highlighting key takeaways.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=179)** They put identified risks and planned actions front and center.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=183)** They planted the report out to leadership and the operations team, setting the stage for transparency.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=190)** Now it's time to share.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=192)** The team lead presents the report to leadership, focusing on impacts and next steps.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=197)** The lead then tailors the message for the operations team and delivers it to them, answering questions and gathering feedback.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=204)** Now that the plan is set, it's time to execute.

> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=212)** William from procurement will confirm SLA details in supplier contracts related to the service, clarifying expectations.

> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=219)** Ted from storage, he'll verify the storage device specifications, ensuring they meet requirements.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=225)** Each will report progress in the next review session: track, adjust, keep moving forward.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=232)** The team checks in on all action items during the all-hands meeting on the 7th, where these discussions naturally fit.
>
> **[3:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=238)** All tasks have been completed as scheduled.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=240)** Gene presents the new router settings, William confirms the SLA details, and Ted reports on the storage specs.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=247)** If roadblocks had come up, they would've adjusted their approach and reassigned tasks as needed to keep momentum going.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=254)** After reviewing progress, the team summarizes key updates and takeaways for stakeholders.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=259)** Gene highlights the router adjustments.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=261)** William shares insights from the SLA review, and Ted outlines storage considerations.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=266)** The team documents lessons learned: what worked, what didn't, and what they'll improve next time.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/brainstorming-example?u=76281980&t=271)** These insights help stakeholders stay informed and guide future decisions.

#### You do it: Brainstorming
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now it's your turn.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=2)** Be sure to separate your brainstorming session into two phases, one that generates ideas and one where you edit, prioritize and select items.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=10)** Use the four dimensions to ensure your approach is holistic.

>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=16)** No idea is criticized ever and everyone contributes in turn and that they follow them.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=23)** Brainstorming, it's not about getting it right, it's about getting it out.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=27)** No filters, no second guessing, just ideas, raw and unpolished, because the best solutions, they don't start perfectly, they start possible.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=35)** So grab a pen, a board, and a voice, whatever works.

>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=40)** No bad ideas, no limits, just thinking forward.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/you-do-it-brainstorming?u=76281980&t=43)** Use the steps you see here to try it now.

### 2. Cause-Effect Analysis

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### What is cause-effect analysis, and why use it?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cause-effect-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cause-effect-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=0)** - Cause-effect analysis is a systematic method you can use to map relationships between causes and effects, making complex issues clearer.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cause-effect-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=9)** Use it to trace back IT service outages or performance issues to the root cause.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cause-effect-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=14)** By visualizing dependencies and failure points, you can communicate problems effectively and take targeted action to prevent recurrence.
>

#### Steps in cause-effect analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The steps in cause-effect analysis are, pick a facilitator, team, and tools, define the problem or effect, draw the fish's trunk and branches, brainstorm causes and relationships, choose actions and set a review date, plan stakeholder communications, communicate findings to stakeholders, take action and track progress, and review progress, adjust, and share updates.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=23)** Pick a facilitator, someone neutral, structured, and focused who can keep discussions on track and ensure everyone contributes.

>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=35)** Choose the right tools or whiteboard, sticky notes, or digital software.

>

>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=73)** If needed, refine the statement together before moving forward, and if possible, prepare the statement before the session.

> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=80)** Here's how to write a good problem statement.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=82)** Write down what's occurring, who's impacted, how, and by how much, and what evidence you have of the impact.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=89)** You'd be surprised how much the problem statement is improved after running it through this process.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=94)** It helps ensure the problem is really a problem and that its up and out impact is understood.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=99)** That's the synthetic view, along with the down and in analytical view.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=105)** Once you've agreed on the problem statement, draw the fish's trunk, an arrow pointing left to right across the middle.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=111)** Make it big enough with enough space above and below it and side to side so the primary and secondary causes will fit.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=119)** Then write the problem statement at its tip.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=122)** Make sure to have access to the detailed problem statement.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=124)** This is critical, the quality of the causes the group will identify hinges on how well the problem statement is articulated and understood.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=133)** Now, draw fish bones, that is arrows pointing at angles to the trunk labeled with the cause categories, the four dimensions as shown here.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=143)** Draw branches, which are the horizontal lines pointing to the bones.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=147)** You'll use these for primary causes.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=150)** Draw stems, arrows pointing to the branches.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=153)** You'll use these for secondary causes.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=157)** You'll likely have some initial primary and secondary causes.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=160)** Write these down, then start the process of brainstorming primary and secondary causes until either participants or ideas are exhausted.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=168)** Under each category, brainstorm all possible causes.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=172)** Ask what contributes to this issue?
>

>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=176)** No filtering yet. Look for patterns and connections.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=180)** If one cause leads to another, draw a secondary branch to show the link.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=184)** This visual mapping will help you uncover root causes, setting the stage for effective solutions.
