>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=196)** Dig deeper until you hit the root cause, not just symptoms.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=200)** If fixing won't prevent recurrence, it's not the root cause.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=205)** Now that you have identified the causes, you must first decide which to investigate.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=210)** Use multivoting to get this done.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=212)** It's a group activity for quickly selecting from a set of options.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=215)** We use it there to select which causes to investigate first.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=219)** Here's how.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=220)** Each person gets a set number of dot stickers or asterisks to draw, and they place them next to the options that they'd like the most.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=228)** Options with the most dots win. That is, they're selected.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=232)** A cause-effect diagram is a valuable artifact, and making one has many benefits.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=236)** The real goal is creating action.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=237)** Action based on the clarity the cause-effect diagram gives you.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=241)** So be sure to capture action items about who will do what and by when as a result of your analysis, instead of date and time for the team to check in on the status of these action items.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=251)** You thoroughly analyze the root causes of the problem, identify the key factors contributing to it, and represented the relationships graphically.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=259)** You've aside actions to mitigate or eliminate causes with owners and timelines established for accountability.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=265)** Now you need to plan what you're going to tell your stakeholders about what you've done, what you'll be doing, and what it means to them.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=272)** Now, tell stakeholders what your findings are, what actions you'll be taking as a result, and the actions to mitigate or eliminate these causes.
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=280)** Tell them that you've assigned owners and timelines in a checkpoint date and that you'll track progress and provide them with updates.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=288)** Now, take action and track progress.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=291)** Use task management tools like Trello, Asana, or a simple action log to track progress and ensure you maintain momentum.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=297)** Doing so helps you achieve what you've set out to do by the review date and turn your ideas into results.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=304)** Where are you?
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=305)** Check progress, are goals on track, deadlines met, what's working?
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=309)** Gather feedback, spot successes, and flag roadblocks.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=314)** What's next? Look at the data.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=316)** Identify gaps and refine actions.
>
> **[5:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=318)** Shift priorities if needed, reassign tasks, and keep moving forward.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=323)** Progress isn't just about speed, it's about direction.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=326)** Adjust, refine, and keep going.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=329)** When you've reviewed progress and made adjustments, when you've learned lessons, don't keep them to yourselves, share them.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-cause-effect-analysis?u=76281980&t=336)** Keep stakeholders in the loop with meetings, reports, or collaboration tools, because progress isn't just made, it's communicated.

### 3. Kepner-Tregoe Root Cause Analysis (RCA)

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Where and when to use Kepner-Tregoe RCA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Use Kepner-Tregoe problem analysis to quickly arrive at a precise problem description, ensuring you identify the true root cause before moving on to solutions.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=10)** Precision is critical, especially in high pressure situations.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=14)** This structured approach helps teams systematically define the what, where, when and extent of the problem.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=21)** Kepner-Tregoe analysis to prioritize and assess facts to prevent jumping to conclusions.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=28)** Don't waste time and resources on solutions that lack a factual basis.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=32)** Use Kepner-Tregoe analysis to help your team focus on verified data to help them avoid misdiagnosing problems, and implementing ineffective action plans.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=42)** The Kepner-Tregoe method provides a shared structure that enables teams to leverage the collective expertise.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=48)** Each steps explicitly integrates different skills, knowledge and experience, ensuring a comprehensive and accurate root cause analysis.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=58)** Kepner-Tregoe analysis helps you break problems into component parts, and produce documentation that records the true cause, and the steps taken to determine it.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=67)** These records are invaluable for organizational learning, future use, and for clearly communicating the nature of a problem when devising solutions.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=75)** Complex problems often involve multiple related effects.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=80)** This approach helps identify who they're connected, distinguishing between primary and secondary issues.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=86)** By doing so, teams can systematically trace each effect back to its cause, and address the most critical factors first.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=93)** In fast-paced environments, where problems must be resolved quickly, which is all environments, Kepner-Tregoe analysis provides a structured way to gather facts, and identify possible causes and solutions efficiently.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=107)** It is especially useful when the issues is ongoing, and requires immediate action.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=112)** Beyond live problem solving, Kepner-Tregoe is also valuable for retrospective analysis.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=117)** Use it in the aftermath of problems to foster organizational learning and improvement.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=122)** By documenting causes and decision paths precisely, teams can improve future processes, refine trouble shooting methods, and enhance overall problem-management strategies.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=132)** When dealing with complex, real time problems, clear communication is essential.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=138)** The Kepner-Tregoe framework provides a structured way to articulate the problem, ensuring that all stakeholders understand the root cause, and the rationale between the chosen solution.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=147)** The strength of Kepner-Tregoe lies in its defined steps and decision gates.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=152)** Each phase must be completed before moving forward, which accelerates rather than slows down the problem-solving process.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=159)** By first identifying the root cause teams can craft targeted solutions that directly address the true issue, yielding far better results than rushed assumption-based fixes.

#### Steps in Kepner-Tregoe RCA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The steps in Kepner-Tregoe analysis are: pick a facilitator team and tools, describe the problem precisely, identify potential causes and evidence, verify true causes and solutions, choose actions and set a review date, plan stakeholder communications, communicate findings to stakeholders, take action and track progress, review progress and adjust as needed, and share updates and lessons learned.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=25)** Start by selecting a facilitator, someone skilled in KT analysis who can guide the team, answer the right questions and keep discussions fact-based.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=34)** Next, assemble a team with deep knowledge of the issue under review.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=38)** Their expertise is key to pinpointing changes and patterns.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=41)** Finally, choose the right tools, structured templates, collaboration platforms and data analysis software to capture insights and drive decisions.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=50)** The right facilitator team and tools ensures a disciplined, effective process.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=55)** Here you develop a precise definition of the problem, including its identity, location, when it occurs and its extent by gathering discrete facts.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=64)** First, its identity.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=66)** The what.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=67)** What exactly is the problem?
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=69)** Then the where.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=71)** Where is the problem located?
>

>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=116)** When you ask what is and what could be but is not for each of these dimensions, be sure to harness the team's knowledge, skills and experience.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=124)** Use the problem description as a basis for rooting out possible causes.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=131)** Your investigation is only as strong as your problem definition.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=134)** Clearly state which deviations from service levels have occurred.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=138)** Often the likely cause is hinted at in the definition, but don't jump to conclusions.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=143)** That can steer the investigation off course.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=146)** Problem definition is tricky.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=147)** IT infrastructure is complex and service agreements aren't always clear.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=151)** Stay precise.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=153)** Define the issue before chasing causes.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=155)** A sharp definition leads to the right solution.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=159)** A key part of this technique in this phase is to ensure that you will find evidence to support or refute each possible cause.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=166)** Zero in on which cause or causes are accurate, which are not and which require more evidence to be gathered to support them.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=173)** In this stage, you test each possible cause to determine whether it could be the cause of all the symptoms of the problem.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=181)** The most likely causes will be those that best explain the is and is not information and have the fewest, most straightforward and reasonable assumptions.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=189)** Test your top suspects.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=191)** Does the cause explain all symptoms?
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=193)** If removing it doesn't fix the issue, refine your list.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=199)** You've ruled out some causes, but a few remain.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=201)** Now, gather the evidence to confirm or eliminate them.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=204)** Test each.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=205)** Does it fully explain the symptoms?
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=207)** Does it fit the is and is not data?
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=209)** Strong candidates require the fewest assumptions and align with the facts.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=212)** If more evidence is needed, go get it.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=215)** Prove or disprove, don't guess.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=217)** The goal, pinpoint the true cause before moving on to solutions to ensure you're solving the right problem.
>
> **[3:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=224)** In this phase, you verify which of the remaining possible causes are the source of the problem.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=229)** A key here is to address the possible causes that could be verified quickly and simply first.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=234)** This is where you look to confirm or refute your assumptions.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=237)** To prove it, you also look to demonstrate and observe the cause-effect relationship at work.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=243)** As a group, you need to be clear up front regarding how you will verify causes and check results.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=249)** You found the cause.
>
> **[4:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=251)** Now, decide what to do.
>

>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=255)** Prioritize impact and urgency.

>

>

>

>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=267)** Who needs to know about what you found out about the problem, its actual cause, and its solution?
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=272)** Who needs to hear that?
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=274)** Anticipate their concerns and build addressing them into your tailored messages.
>

>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=280)** Transparency builds trust.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=282)** A strong communication plan is especially important after an impactful problem has been resolved.
>

>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=290)** Fact-based, focus, and to the point.
>

>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=299)** Address concerns up front.
>

>

>

>

>

>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=322)** Success isn't just about action, it's about the right action.

> **[5:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=330)** If not, find out why.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=332)** Adapt, refine, and improve.

>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=337)** The key, continuous assessment until you've proven the fix is stuck.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=342)** Once you've confirmed that the fix is stuck, wrap things up, but don't close the book just yet.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=347)** Share outcomes, what worked, what didn't, and why.

> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=351)** Capture and share lessons for a better future, because the best problem solvers don't just fix issues, they make the whole system smarter.

#### Example of Kepner-Tregoe RCA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now that you've seen the steps to Kepner-Tregoe analysis, let's examine a real-world example to help you understand what you've learned.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=7)** The service desk indicates that the users of the collaboration service are reporting poor performance.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=12)** The IT team responsible for the collaboration service at Nexa CoLab is struggling to identify and fix the cause of poor performance.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=20)** A SWAT team is assembled to go after the problem.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=22)** Alex, the IT manager, takes charge of the investigation and facilitates the problem analysis, Priya from the engineering team takes on infrastructure diagnostics, while Jordan from AppDev focuses on app logs, and Chris from the database team will check database performance.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=38)** The team decides to use monitoring dashboards, logs, and packet captures to pinpoint the issue.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=44)** Priya begins pulling historical trends and checking server load.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=49)** The team assembles to go after the problem.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=51)** It uses a Kepner-Tregoe problem analysis template to gather the facts.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=55)** There is poor performance, but isn't an outage.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=58)** The problem seems isolated to Legato developer team sites, but not business-facing collaboration sites.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=64)** There's no clear pattern to the performance issues.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=67)** All Legato team members are affected.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=69)** File uploads, downloads, and process workflows are timing out, and list views are freezing and not rendering.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=76)** Interestingly, there's been no impact on timer jobs.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=80)** The team now discusses possible causes and provides evidence to support or refute the potential causes.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=86)** They quickly come up with a list of possible causes, from inadequate hardware to Active Directory issues, and keep all but one of them, which they discard due to a lack of evidence to support it.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=98)** Now the team turns to identifying and running tests for each possible cause to determine whether it could be the cause of all the symptoms of the problem.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=106)** They look for the most likely causes, those that best explain the is and is not information, and that have the fewest and most straightforward and reasonable assumptions.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=117)** Through this process, they eliminate several causes from consideration, including bad topology, customization issues, overlapping timer jobs, and bugs.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=127)** Now, the team turns its attention to the causes that have not been eliminated and plan out how they will verify or refute the remaining possible causes to narrow down to the one actual cause of the problem.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=139)** They want to address the possible causes that can be verified quickly and simply first, so they start with inadequate hardware.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=147)** After a quick check using the usage, health data, and health analyzer, they eliminate inadequate hardware as a possible cause because they saw no evidence to support it in their verification tests.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=158)** Another part of the team simultaneously checks the large/wide list views theory.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=163)** This also comes up short.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=167)** Another part of the team, dispatched to check log files for database, directory services, and crawl logs, immediately finds some significant weirdness going on and verifies that these issues are the true cause of the performance degradation.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=179)** They test the solution that proves it removes the issues.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=184)** The team went from problem to actual cause to solution, fast and focused, using the Kepner-Tregoe method.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=190)** They moved step by step, precise problem definition, potential causes, evidence gathering, and verification of the true cause and solution.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=198)** No guessing, no wasted effort, just a precise, logical analysis.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=202)** And now, the true cause and solution are confirmed.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=206)** The team chooses, prioritizes, and assign actions, who, what, and when, actions that will fix the issues.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=212)** They're moving quickly and will make the fix as soon as possible and will review performance in two hours and again the following day, escalating if they find the fix does not resolve the performance issues.
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=223)** The problem-solving team determines that they must inform Legato teams about the issues and the fix.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=228)** They plan to notify leadership and the service desk to manage expectations.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=232)** They specifically include a note that some Legato users may experience brief slowness while the fix is being applied.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=239)** The team informs Legato leadership that the issue has been pinpointed and the fix is underway.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=244)** They update the service desk, ensuring that users receive communication about the active resolution and a confirmation once performance is back to normal.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=253)** The team initiates the fix, estimating a completion time of one hour and 45 minutes.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=257)** They engage in real-time performance tracking to monitor response times during the transition.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=262)** They observe that the performance metrics are on the uptick.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=266)** They stay on it to validate results before marking the issue as resolved.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=270)** The team confirms that fixes are complete and reports that latency has dropped to within the desired levels.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=276)** They test list views and confirm their load instantly.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=279)** They verify that query performance now matches that of the business-facing sites.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=283)** They confirm success, but schedule an additional 24-hour heightened monitoring period before closing the issue, just to be sure.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=291)** The team provides stakeholders with an update, confirming that the Legato users' performance has returned to normal and identifying the root cause and its fix.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-kepner-tregoe-rca?u=76281980&t=300)** They outlined safeguards being added to configuration guidelines and testing policies to prevent similar issues in the future, and document the fix in postmortem logs for future reference.

### 4. Fault Tree Analysis (FTA)

#### What is fault tree analysis, and why use it?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=0)** - Fault tree analysis is a technique for identifying the chain of events that has caused or may cause a problem such as a service outage or a performance degradation.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=10)** Fault tree analysis links basic, resultant, conditional, and trigger events using bullion logic operators, and, or, exor and the like to illustrate chains of events and the logic behind them graphically.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=24)** Why use fault tree analysis?
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=26)** Because guessing isn't a strategy.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=28)** Fault tree analysis traces failure step by step, revealing cause and effect chains and hidden dependencies.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=34)** It pinpoints risks helping you prevent future issues before they even happen.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-fault-tree-analysis-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=39)** Want clear insights, smarter decisions, stronger systems?

#### Steps in fault tree analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The steps in fault-tree analysis are, pick a facilitator, team, and tools.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=4)** Define the top, base, and resulting events.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=7)** Combine events with logic and check.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=10)** Evaluate probability and risk, and develop countermeasures.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=13)** Choose actions instead of review date.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=15)** Plan stakeholder communication.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=18)** Communicate findings to stakeholders.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=20)** Take action and track progress.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=21)** Review progress, adjust as needed.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=23)** And share updates and lessons learned.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=27)** Combinations of failure that could lead to a specific system-level fault or undesired event don't identify themselves.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=34)** Pick a neutral and sharp facilitator who knows the technique and can facilitate a team.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=39)** Create a team with the right mix of skills, people who know the system and can connect the dots.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=44)** Choose tools like whiteboards and fault-tree-diagramming software.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=47)** With the right people and tools, you're ready for success.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=51)** Fault-tree analysis identifies the faults and logical relationships among faults that lead to an event.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=57)** In the context of problem management, the top event we're concerned with, is the failure or degradation of an IT service.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=63)** Define the top event as clearly as possible.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=65)** For example, SAN 1 is unavailable in LAN segment two at 2:00 PM.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=70)** Here's a tip, make it a synopsis of a precise problem description captured using Kepner-Tregoe analysis.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=78)** To do fault-tree analysis, write your top-level event, then events leading to it, and connect them with logic gates.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=85)** Continue writing levels of events that lead to the higher level intermediate events and connect them with logic gates until you get to the bottom of the tree.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=93)** You'll know you're there as these essential events have two characteristics in common.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=97)** They require no further investigation, and you can establish a countermeasure for them.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=103)** Identify the necessary and sufficient events to cause the top events directly.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=108)** These are the intermediate events.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=111)** Look for base and resulting events in the four dimensions, in organizations and people, in who is responsible, how teams interact, and where human errors may contribute.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=120)** In information and technology, and data flows, dependencies, and potential IT failures.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=125)** In partners and suppliers, third-party risks, service agreements, and external dependencies.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=131)** And in value streams and processes, and how work flows and where weaknesses exist, and which processes could break.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=138)** Here's where we identify how events relate.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=142)** To review with an AND gate, the resulting event only occurs when all input events coincide.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=148)** For example, you can only turn on a light if there's a working bulb in it, and the outlet the light is connected to has power.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=155)** With an OR gate, the resulting event occurs when one or more input events occur.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=160)** For instance, an outlet will not have power if either the building or the circuit breaker for that outlet has tripped.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=166)** With an XOR gate or Exclusive OR gate, the resulting event occurs when one and only one of the input events occur.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=173)** With the INHIBIT gate, the resulting event only occurs when both inputs occur, and an external condition event also occurs.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=182)** Use logical operators to represent how failures interact.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=185)** AND gates require multiple failures to occur together, while OR gates indicate alternative paths leading to failure.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=192)** This step helps accurately model how the system breaks down.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=196)** Review the tree to confirm logical accuracy.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=199)** Ensure events are correctly connected, with AND, and OR, and other gates properly applied.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=204)** This prevents false conclusions, and guarantees that failure pathways reflect real-world conditions.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=211)** Root-cause events are those that do not require further investigation, and for which you can establish a countermeasure.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=217)** For example, a switch is stuck in the on position.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=221)** Here, we see that lamps one and two could be burned out, and there's no voltage on the network or a fuse burned out as root cause events.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=229)** These essential events sit at the bottom of the fault tree, and are depicted with an ovals.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=235)** Now, you need to understand and record the probability and impact of each root cause, and the cost and effort required to address it.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=242)** You can use a numeric scale and multi-voting as described in the brainstorming segment.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=246)** For example, one is high probability, impact, cost, and effort.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=250)** Five is low probability, impact, cost, and effort.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=253)** For each root cause, you'll have four numbers to calculate its weight, probability, impact, cost, and effort.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=261)** Now, identify countermeasures, mitigations, and contingencies.
>
> **[4:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=264)** So, for example, if a root cause is the failure of a power supply, adding a redundant power supply would be a countermeasure.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=271)** It's a specific type of countermeasure, a mitigation.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=274)** Remember, mitigations are countermeasures that minimize or eliminate a fault.
>
> **[4:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=278)** Contingencies, the other kind of countermeasure, are things you put in place to recover quickly should the fault occur.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=285)** Using a spreadsheet, brainstorm countermeasures and weigh them by probability, impact of failure, and cost and effort to fix them.
>
> **[4:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=292)** All other things being equal, those failures with the highest probability, the highest impact, and the lowest cost and effort, should be listed first.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=300)** In this part of the process, you establish countermeasures, mitigations, and contingencies.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=304)** Weigh them, and select a subset of the highest value countermeasures to act on.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=308)** First, identify high-risk failures and implement redundancy, like backup power for critical systems.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=314)** Next, failure likelihood can be reduced by monitoring to catch early warning signs.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=319)** Then set up contingencies, such as failover procedures to reroute traffic if a network link goes down.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=325)** Finally, document and test.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=327)** Run simulation drills to ensure your mitigations work.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=331)** Have a plan for every risk to prevent, detect, or recover from failure.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=336)** The main objective of all this work is to produce a list of action items, including who will do what by when.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=342)** Choose the top 20 or less percent of the countermeasures you've identified to focus your efforts.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=346)** Then assign who will do what by when in the way of improvement initiatives.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=351)** Set a review date to check in on progress and help ensure accountability.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=355)** Plan stakeholder communications to keep everyone informed, aligned, and confident.
>
> **[6:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=360)** Let the right people know what happened, what's being done, and what to expect next.
>
> **[6:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=365)** Identify stakeholders, such as leaders, teams, and customers, and tailor messages for each.
>
> **[6:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=370)** Use the right credible messengers and channels, the ones they use, like email, meetings, or dashboards.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=376)** Keep it concise, actionable, transparent, and bidirectional to get the feedback you need.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=381)** Share your decisions with your stakeholders, summarizing chosen actions, explaining your rationale, and indicating who will do what by when.
>
> **[6:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=389)** Remember, your goal is to improve reality by making improvements and to influence your stakeholder's perceptions through your communications.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=397)** Use task-management tools like Trello, Asana, or a simple action log to track progress and ensure you maintain momentum.
>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=404)** Achieve your goals by the review date, and turn your ideas into results.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=410)** You've identified single points of failure, you've tackled weak points, but is the job done?
>
> **[6:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=415)** Check progress.
>
> **[6:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=416)** Have the impacts of those failures been eliminated, mitigated, or do gaps remain?
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=422)** Test resilience, validate fixes, adjust where needed.
>
> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=425)** Because closing a single point of failure isn't just a task, it's a transformation.
>
> **[7:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=430)** Review, refine, fortify, keep strengthening.
>
> **[7:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=434)** Progress matters, but so does visibility.
>
> **[7:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=437)** Stakeholders need to know, what's fixed?
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=439)** How will the fix improve uptime?
>
> **[7:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=441)** What's still at risk, what's next?
>
> **[7:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=443)** Deliver clear updates through reports, meetings, and dashboards.
>
> **[7:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=446)** Show impact, highlight improvements, address concerns.
>
> **[7:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=450)** Because trust's built through transparency, and resilience is strengthened when everyone's aligned.

#### Example of fault tree analysis

>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=52)** The team then identifies necessary and sufficient events to directly cause a top event.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=56)** In this case, a failure of either the SQL server or DNS will cause the failure of the SharePoint collaboration service.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=63)** The team continues to identify events that lead to other events that eventually lead to the failure of the SharePoint collaboration service.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=71)** The team continues to identify events that lead to other events that eventually lead to the failure of the SharePoint collaboration service and to connect them with Logic Gates.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=80)** Here we see a part of their work where they identified two events, either of which could cause DNS to be down, so they connect them with an OR gate.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=89)** The team proceeds until they reach the root cause events, which do not require further investigation and for which you can establish a countermeasure.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=97)** In this example, either the server being down, the server's network interface card being disabled, or the network that the server's attached to being down could cause the server to appear offline.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=108)** Now the team assesses the probability and impact of each root cause and the cost and effort required to address it.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-fault-tree-analysis?u=76281980&t=115)** They use a spreadsheet to do this.

>

### 5. Component Failure Impact Analysis (CFIA)

#### What is CFIA, and why use it?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cfia-and-why-use-it?u=76281980)

>

> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cfia-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=10)** Does it slow down, crash, adapt?

>

>

>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cfia-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=54)** Use it to identify single points of failure, evaluate risk and impact, and justify countermeasures to reduce exposure.

>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-cfia-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=65)** Stay ahead of failure through component failure impact analysis.

#### Where and when to use CFIA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Use component failure impact analysis to identify items that can cause outages, especially single points of failure.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=7)** Apply it during system design after incidents, or before major upgrades.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=13)** Focus on critical dependencies, power, networking databases, and authentication services.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=20)** If one fails, what's the impact?
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=23)** If it's high, add redundancy, monitoring and failover capability.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=29)** Use component failure impact analysis to break down a service into its configuration items and assess the risk of failure.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=36)** Apply it during design reviews, risk assessments, or after outages.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=42)** Look at servers, databases, integrations and dependencies.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=45)** What happens if one fails?
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=48)** Identify weak points, assess impact and prioritize countermeasures.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=54)** Use component failure impact analysis to build a data-driven case for countermeasure investments.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=60)** Apply it when requesting funding for redundancy, monitoring or failover systems.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=65)** Show the cost of downtime versus the cost of prevention.

> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=74)** Decision makers to respond to clear evidence so make it easy for them to say yes.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-cfia?u=76281980&t=81)** Use component failure impact analysis early in service and process development to design for reliability.

#### Example of CFIA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Now that you've seen the steps to component failure impact analysis, let's explore a real world example to reinforce what you've learned.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=8)** The entire organization at Nexa Colab relies on a collaboration service for meetings, messaging, and file sharing.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=15)** But what happens if it fails?
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=17)** Today, the team is running a component failure impact analysis to find out.
>

> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=26)** The goal, minimize downtime, and keep communication flowing.

>

> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=77)** There is some back and forth here because of some unevenness.

>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=93)** Also, some SANs have an active active configuration where others have an active passive configuration.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-cfia?u=76281980&t=100)** So the team makes some notes in addition to marking up the spreadsheet with S's, A's H's, W's, and C's, because all of this is relevant to the analysis.

> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-cfia?u=76281980&t=146)** Show the value.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-cfia?u=76281980&t=148)** When CFIA prevents downtime or speeds up recovery, highlight those wins to cement adoption.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-cfia?u=76281980&t=155)** Now you understand what component failure impact analysis is, why to use it, where to apply it, and how to execute it, hopefully you've tried the technique, reflected on the experience, and learned something useful for you and your team moving forward.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-cfia?u=76281980&t=170)** In the next movie, you'll learn about service outage analysis.

### 6. Service Outage Analysis (SOA)

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### What is SOA, and why use it?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-soa-and-why-use-it?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-soa-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=0)** - Service outage analysis is a technique for examining past outages to identify the most significant and addressable contributors to their occurrence and duration, including people, processes, products, technologies, and partners, which are suppliers or vendors.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-soa-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=16)** The goal of service outage analysis is to reduce the risk and time to recover from potential future outages.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-soa-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=23)** Service outage analysis isn't just about what went wrong, it's about making sure it doesn't happen again.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-soa-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=29)** Every outage holds valuable insights.

>

>

>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/what-is-soa-and-why-use-it?u=76281980&t=73)** Outages will happen.
