#### Where and when to use SOA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Want to reduce outages?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=2)** Start by understanding them.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=4)** Use service outage analysis to pinpoint what caused past outages and how long they lasted.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=10)** Use it after major incidents to find root causes and trends.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=13)** Use it to improve reliability, the time between service failures, and maintainability, how fast you can restore service.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=22)** Service outage analysis isn't just about the past.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=25)** Use it regularly to predict and prevent future failures, to spot outage patterns, weak points in infrastructure, and risks that could lead to repeat failures.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=35)** Use it to look for trends in component failures, delays in recovery, and recurring service disruptions.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=41)** Address these risks before they cause outages to improve service, reliability, maintainability, and resilience.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=49)** Service outage analysis isn't just about understanding failures; it's about preventing them and improving your response when they do occur.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=56)** Use it after every major incident to identify root causes, recurring issues, and gaps in recovery processes.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=64)** Regular reviews will help you fix weak points before they cause bigger problems and refine incident response playbooks to recover faster next time.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=74)** Use service outage analysis to spot patterns and past failures and take action to reduce both how often outages happen and how long they last.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=83)** After every outage, analyze what failed, why, and how quickly services were restored.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=89)** Identify repeat failure points and slow recovery steps, then prioritize fixes.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=95)** Over time, you'll reduce outage frequency by improving reliability and shorten downtime by streamlining recovery.
>

>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=108)** Use service outage analysis to find delays.
>

>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=115)** Look for patterns like missing runbooks, slow escalations, or unclear roles.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-soa?u=76281980&t=121)** Fix these with better documentation, automation, and training to speed recovery.

#### Steps in SOA
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The steps in service outage analysis are select a facilitator, team, and tools, group and filter outages, group and filter causes, examine downtime duration reasons and trends in similar outages, choose actions and set a review date, plan stakeholder communications, communicate findings to stakeholders, take action and track progress, review progress and adjust as needed, and share updates and lessons learned.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=26)** Start by choosing a facilitator, someone neutral with subject matter expertise who also has the skills to guide the discussion and keep it on task.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=34)** Assemble a cross-functional team with technical expertise and stakeholders.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=38)** To ensure a structured approach, pick the right tools and data and prepare them in advance, such as instant logs, monitoring data, and root cause analysis frameworks.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=47)** First, choose a set of related outages you want to analyze.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=51)** You can group outages for analysis by any criteria you find helpful.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=54)** For example, you can group by supplier, product, service, application, customer, platform, region, or period.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=62)** Look for patterns.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=63)** Which outages are related?
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=65)** Group them by shared causes or affected systems, then focus on the major ones with the biggest impact on users or business operations.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=73)** Don't waste time on minor blips that don't reveal systemic issues.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=78)** Now tag the most significant outages so you can focus your analysis on them to make the most of your time and effort.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=85)** Typically, the most considerable outages have had the most extended duration and/or impact on the business.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=90)** Apply the Pareto principle, focusing on the 20% of the outages that create 80% of the impact.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=96)** For the significant outages, list the causes in each of the four dimensions.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=100)** You may find that the majority of the outages result from one category or set of causes.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=106)** Break down each outage.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=107)** Where was the delay?
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=109)** Detection, diagnosis, execution?
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=112)** Look for trends in similar incidents.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=115)** If recovery always takes too long, is it a process issue, a tooling gap, or a skill shortage?
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=121)** Address the patterns.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=124)** Apply the 80/20 rule and focus on identifying improvement action items for the 20% of causes that cause 80% of the outages.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=130)** For these causes, identify action items to address avoidable causes, where avoidable means a cause you can do something about.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=138)** Aim to identify action items to reduce recovery time from service outages.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=143)** For the significant outages, list primary contributors to the duration of the outages.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=148)** Often, outage resolutions share a set of key contributors to the time it takes to restore service after an interruption.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=155)** What you're trying to do here is to crash the cycle time required to recover from an outage.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=159)** It's a good practice to map out all the components of the cycle time, like the time to detect, identify the problem, resolve it, and so on.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=166)** And look for each element to find action items to reduce it.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=171)** List potential action items to reduce outage frequency and duration.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=175)** Quantify the potential impacts the action items will have on reducing the frequency and duration of outages.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=180)** You should be able to draw this out of your data.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=182)** For example, if a particular outage dragged on because it took an hour to find the documentation for a component, locating it in your knowledge library for the service will take an hour out of the future outage durations for similar problems.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=194)** Your goal is to choose action items that will eliminate any avoidable outage time.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=199)** As you don't have unlimited time and resources, select the subset of action items that are potentially the most impactful and set the rest aside.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=206)** All other things being equal, rank items that are easy to do, require little or no resources, and have a higher impact on reducing the frequency and duration of outages higher than items that are hard, time-consuming, and costly to do, and have a low impact on outages.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=221)** Assign owners, set deadlines, and schedule a review date to check progress.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=226)** Decide who needs to know what and when.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=228)** Senior leadership wants business impact insights.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=231)** Engineering needs technical takeaways.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=234)** End users may need reassurance.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=236)** Tailor messages so each group gets what they need, no more, no less.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=241)** Communicate to ensure that key stakeholders, the customers, users, IT staff, relevant suppliers, and so on, know your findings and planned action items.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=249)** Let them know you did the analysis and the actions you're taking.
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=253)** Take care when communicating your action's potential contribution to reducing the frequency and duration of future problems.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=258)** A good rule of thumb is to cut the quantities you expect in half and to use those numbers so you underpromise and overdeliver.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=267)** Follow through.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=268)** Make sure assigned actions are being executed.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=270)** Use dashboards, check-ins, or reports to track progress.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=273)** Analysis without action does not lead to improvement, and improvement is what we're all about here.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=279)** Are the fixes working?
>
> **[4:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=280)** Have outages decreased?
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=282)** If not, why not?

> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=285)** Maybe the problem was misunderstood or the solution needs tweaking.

> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-soa?u=76281980&t=288)** Regularly review progress to ensure continuous improvement.

>

>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=98)** The facilitator ensures that data was available for all outages under consideration in advance, so the team didn't have to dig for it in the meeting.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=106)** Notice that lack of experience on Azure versions of services, DNS, and active directory has contributed to most of these outages.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=114)** So the team focuses on these since they aim to focus on the 20% of causes that cause 80% of the outages.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=122)** The team sees that recent outages in the collaboration service saw extended recovery times due to three key issues, and AD network and VLAN config change added 45 minutes as teams diagnosed authentication failures.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=135)** A firewall change delayed recovery by 30 minutes due to unexpected access control issues.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=141)** A DNS propagation error caused intermittent disruptions, adding 60 minutes before resolution.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=147)** Each case highlights the need for tighter change coordination, faster rollback execution, and improved validation steps to reduce downtime.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=156)** The team brainstorms action items to address the root causes of the significant outages and comes up with a list shown here.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=163)** They prioritize the actions based on the impact of each root cause against the effort and cost to address them.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=169)** A process compliance discussion with the vendor bubbled to the top, because it was easy to do and should have a high impact.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=175)** Next came AD team training on Azure AD and Azure DNS training.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=180)** The sequence here was chosen because Azure AD issues had contributed more to outages than Azure DNS.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=190)** Now, the team looks at each improvement action and estimates how much time will be cut out of the recovery cycle by implementing it.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=197)** As you can see, most of the avoidable recovery time was in the diagnosis phase.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=201)** With a lack of understanding of Azure AD, the key contributor, and a lack of DNS experience coming in a close second, the team agrees on the time that would be cut out of the recovery cycle after implementing the action.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=213)** They agree further that when communicating to stakeholders, they will have their estimates to ensure they under promise and over deliver.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=220)** There's a dollar cost to two of these action items, so the facilitator representing the team puts these costs in front of the head of IT for approval.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=228)** If a change was required, like replacing network switches or adjusting default switch settings, the change manager would've been involved and a change request would've been necessary, but there wasn't, so the team moves on.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=241)** The team now sets a date to check in on action items.
>

>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=259)** All SharePoint users and a subset of developers, the legato developers, were impacted by five outages that could have been in scope.
>
> **[4:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=266)** Now, the team wants to communicate tailored messages based on the results of their analysis.

> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=271)** The head of the AD team and enterprise directory services will communicate results to the IT staff, and the head of the service desk will communicate results to customers and users.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=281)** The head of the AD team shares findings with the IT staff, detailing how directory services dependencies contributed to outages and outlining technical improvements to prevent recurrence.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=291)** Meanwhile, the head of the service desk informs users and developers, explaining the impact on SharePoint and legato services, what has been resolved and what's being done to improve reliability.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=301)** Each message is tailored to ensure stakeholders understand the root causes, corrective actions, and next steps.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=310)** The AD team completes training on Azure AD, ensuring they can better manage directory dependencies.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=315)** The vendor compliance discussion takes place, addressing requirements to prevent future disruptions.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=320)** Meanwhile, the network team undergoes Azure DNS training to improve troubleshooting and configuration practices.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-soa?u=76281980&t=327)** Each team tracks progress reports updates and ensures these actions strengthen system reliability.

> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-soa?u=76281980&t=58)** These skills improve with practice.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-soa?u=76281980&t=60)** Your goal is to spot patterns, refined processes, and strengthen response strategies.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-soa?u=76281980&t=65)** Triage.

> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-soa?u=76281980&t=66)** Quickly and systematically assess outages to pinpoint the most effective ways to prevent recurrence and speed up resolution when problems do occur.

#### Where and when to use a problem review
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-a-problem-review?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Solving problems isn't enough.

> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/where-and-when-to-use-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=2)** You must learn from them.

#### Steps in a problem review
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The steps in a problem review are, select a facilitator, team, and tools.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=4)** Agree roles, objectives, summary, timeline, and root cause.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=8)** Agree what went well and what needs improvement.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=11)** Document lessons learned.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=13)** Choose action items and set a review date.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=16)** Plan stakeholder communication.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=18)** Communicate findings to stakeholders.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=20)** Take action and track progress.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=22)** Review progress and adjust as needed, and share updates and lessons learned.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=28)** Start by choosing a neutral facilitator, someone who can guide discussions and keep the review fact-based.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=34)** Someone who can focus the team on learning and improvement and facilitate crisp, convincing communications with stakeholders.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=42)** Select the right team to participate in the problem review.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=45)** Include anyone who can contribute significantly to the understanding and communication of the problem and its handling or action items for continual improvement.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=53)** Ensure participants in the problem review clearly understand the three outcomes you're shooting for.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=60)** First, to understand as a group why the problem happened, and determine if it can be prevented from recurring if at all possible.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=67)** Second, to determine how the problem was handled and to determine what can be put in place to better handle a similar future problem.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=75)** Third, to agree on action items and a communication plan to key stakeholders.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=81)** Then choose the right tools, whiteboards, shared documents, or digital collaboration platforms to capture insights and keep everyone aligned.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=91)** Gather facts and opinions before the problem review workshop.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=94)** Use the four dimensions to group data into categories.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=97)** Here's a tip on ensuring you've got the essential data for the meeting.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=100)** Ask yourself if any data could cause the meeting to grind to a halt if you don't have it, then make sure you've got that data ready to hand at the meeting.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=110)** You want to make sure the discussion is fact-based.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=113)** Still, you'll also want qualitative data such as the customer's opinions on the impacts of the problem on business operation, and how the situation was handled.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=122)** Remember, your twin goals are to get a better reality and perception.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=126)** These goals require both facts and opinions to be acknowledged, surfaced, and handled.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=133)** To ensure you keep the agenda on schedule, be sure to time box out each agenda item in proportion to its size, and make sure participants know the time allocated for each upfront.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=143)** Use a parking lot to park ideas that come up that are worth having a look at later offline, but need to be parked now so you can progress against the agenda in the allotted time.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=153)** Remember that the primary purpose of the review is not to try to get perfect data and perfect communications and action items.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=159)** Instead, it's for the team to learn and initiate action items and communications together promptly to move the dial and understanding and improvement in the right direction, and to keep key stakeholders informed.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=170)** Clarify roles so that everyone knows their part, who leads, documents and analyzes.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=175)** Define the objective.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=177)** Are you preventing recurrence, improving response, or both?
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=180)** Summarize the issue, establish a timeline and agree on the problem and root cause statements, ensuring everyone is aligned on the facts before diving into solutions.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=190)** Next, cover problem handling.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=192)** What went well, not so well?
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=194)** What action items can you take to handle the problem better next time?
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=199)** Highlight successes, not just failures.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=201)** What worked?
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=202)** How can you build on that?
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=204)** What didn't work, and how can you improve on it?
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=207)** Ask after gaps in detection, response, and resolution.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=210)** Be constructive and solution-focused.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=212)** Don't place blame.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=214)** Balance accountability with the safety to admit failures so you can learn and grow.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=220)** What did you learn about the cause of the problem and how you handled it?
>
> **[3:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=223)** Write down key takeaways, insights on what worked, what failed and why.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=228)** Keep your documentation clear and actionable so that future teams can benefit.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=233)** Avoid over-articulating or using vague statements.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=235)** Focus on practical, specific lessons that you and others can use to drive meaningful improvements.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=242)** What action items will you take as a result of your learning to eliminate the problem from recurring?
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=247)** What will you do to minimize the impact of the problem by putting things in place to handle it better, should it reoccur?
>
> **[4:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=253)** Record action items in this step, including the who, what, and by when?
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=257)** Turn lessons into actions.
>
> **[4:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=259)** Prioritize tasks based on impact, probability and effort.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=262)** Assign owners, set deadlines, and ensure every action has a clear path forward.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=267)** Without action, lessons learned become lessons lost.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=273)** Stakeholder trust depends on clear, strategic communication.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=276)** First, identify them, customers, users, IT teams, executives, who has a stake in the problem and its solution?
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=283)** Next, tell your message.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=285)** What happened, what's being done, and what it means for them.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=289)** Keep it clear and relevant.
>
> **[4:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=291)** Then choose the right messengers and channels, credibility and delivery matter.
>
> **[4:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=297)** Finally, reinforce confidence, show you understand the problem.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=300)** Explain how you will prevent or minimize the impact of future issues.
>
> **[5:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=306)** Present the problem review's conclusions clearly.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=308)** Explain what happened, what's being done, what to expect next, what it means, and what is in it for the stakeholder.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=315)** Keep communications focused and actionable.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=319)** Start executing.
>
> **[5:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=320)** Monitor progress, remove blockers, and ensure tasks move forward.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=325)** Monitoring and adjusting based on what you see prevents momentum from stalling.
>
> **[5:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=328)** This allows you to turn insights into improvements.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=331)** All the work you've done up to this point will be for nothing if no action is taken based on the lessons you've learned.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=337)** Aim to finish all assigned tasks in advance of the checkpoint review.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=342)** Now, conduct a checkpoint review to review plan versus completed tasks.
>
> **[5:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=347)** Adjust if necessary, things change and so should the plan.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=350)** Check what's working, what's stalled, and where adjustments are needed.
>
> **[5:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=354)** Flexibility is key.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=355)** If a solution isn't working, tweak it before it's too late.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=359)** Update stakeholders on your progress on promised improvement action items, including any adjustments between planned and actual tasks completed.
>
> **[6:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=367)** Wrap it up by sharing what's changed, what's improved, and what still needs work.
>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=372)** This ensures continuous learning and reinforces a culture of problem solving.
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/steps-in-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=377)** Make insights accessible so the next team doesn't have to start from scratch.

#### Example of a problem review
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] Now that you've seen the steps to problem review, let's explore a real-world example to reinforce your learning.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=7)** The collaboration service recently experienced an extended outage of about four hours during peak business hours.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=13)** While the service was back up and running, many people were upset about the outage and wanted to know what the IT team was doing and what they would do to prevent it from happening again.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=23)** Alex, the incident response lead, will facilitate a problem review.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=28)** It's already known that the outage was due to VLAN changes affecting directory services.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=33)** Alex invites enterprise directory design team members directly involved in the problem resolution.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=38)** She also invites the vendor team who were engaged in the VLAN changes that contributed to the outage.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=43)** She invites the change enablement lead and another supplier, Microsoft, to bring knowledge of Azure AD.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=50)** She aims to get the right perspectives in the room without filling with too many people.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=54)** She has to decide whether some individuals will be invited or represented in the session.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=60)** Alex gets a review date and a location set.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=63)** She uses the standard problem review agenda shown here.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=67)** First, problem review, second, problem handling review, then action item review, and finally, communication planning.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=75)** The team gathers key tools and data to piece together what happened.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=79)** They analyzed logs, network authentication, firewall, and collaboration service logs.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=84)** They review VLAN configurations, change records, and system health dashboards.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=89)** They pull data from monitoring tools, alerts, and CMDV records to track dependencies.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=95)** User reported incidents, help desk tickets, and synthetic tests revealed the impact.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=100)** They've reconstructed timeline using conferencing tools, escalation records, and service maps.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=108)** The team gathers qualitative and quantitative data on the problem's root causes and the problem recovery cycle.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=114)** It's clear what the root cause of the outage was, the VLAN config change, so there's not much digging to do.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/example-of-a-problem-review?u=76281980&t=119)** However, some strong opinions about the vendor team's contribution to the problem have been expressed.
>

> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=53)** What worked and what didn't.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=56)** Some teams struggle to identify key stakeholders and tailor messages.
>

>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=62)** What's improving?
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=63)** How does it affect them?
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=65)** Missed stakeholders risk dissatisfaction.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=68)** Clear communication is critical.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=71)** How is participation?
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=73)** Those closest to the problem are likely most engaged, focused on accurate review, prevention and improvement.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=80)** Did anyone have a breakthrough?

>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=86)** Did anyone gain a new perspective?
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=89)** Now we return to the key question, will you implement this technique in your organization?
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=95)** You may already be using a similar approach for specific problems.

>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/putting-itil-into-practice-problem-management-techniques-25083448/review-it-problem-review?u=76281980&t=111)** So there you have it.
